                  <foreign lang="ar">عُقُود</foreign>; (A, K;) with <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>, (Msb,) and with fet-h to the <foreign lang="ar">ش</foreign>, (TA,) for the masc.; (Msb, TA;) and <foreign lang="ar">عَشْرٌ</foreign>, without <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>, (Msb, TA,) and with one fet-hah, (TA,) for the fem. (Msb, TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">عَشَرَةُ رِجَالٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Ten men</hi>]: and <foreign lang="ar">عَشْرُ نِسْوَةٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">ten women</hi>]. (S, O, Msb, TA.) [In De Sacy's Arabic Grammar, for the former is inadvertently put <foreign lang="ar">عَشْرَةٌ</foreign>; and for the latter, <foreign lang="ar">عَشَرٌ</foreign>; and in Freytag's lexicon we find <foreign lang="ar">عَشَرٌ</foreign> instead of <foreign lang="ar">عَشْرٌ</foreign>.] <foreign lang="ar">عَشَرَاتٌ</foreign> [is the pl. of <foreign lang="ar">عَشَرَةٌ</foreign>: and also] signifies <hi rend="ital">Decimal numbers.</hi> (M in art. <foreign lang="ar">ست</foreign>.) The vulgar make <foreign lang="ar">عَشْرٌ</foreign> masc., as meaning a number of days, saying <foreign lang="ar">العَشْرُ الأَوَّلُ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">العَشْرُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الأَخِيرُ</foreign>; but this is wrong [unless thereby they mean to speak of nights with their days, as will be shown by what follows]: the month consists of three <foreign lang="ar">عَشَرَات</foreign>; namely, <foreign lang="ar">العَشْرُ الأُوَلُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The first ten</hi> nights. with their days], pl. of <foreign lang="ar">أُولَى</foreign>; and <foreign lang="ar">العَشْرُ الوُسَطُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The middle ten</hi> nights, with their days], pl. of <foreign lang="ar">وُسْطَى</foreign>; and <foreign lang="ar">العَشْرُ الأَخَرُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The last,</hi> lit. <hi rend="ital">the other, ten</hi> nights, with their days], pl. of <foreign lang="ar">أُخْرَى</foreign>; or <foreign lang="ar">العَشْرُ الأَوَاخِرُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The last ten</hi> nights, with their days], pl. of <foreign lang="ar">آخرَةٌ</foreign>. (Msb.) [<foreign lang="ar">العَشْرُ الأَوَاخِرُ</foreign> is also especially applied to <hi rend="ital">The last ten</hi> nights of Ramadán, with their days: and <foreign lang="ar">عَشْرُ ذِى الحِجَّةِ</foreign> to <hi rend="ital">The</hi> first <hi rend="ital">ten</hi> nights <hi rend="ital">of Dhu-l-Hijjeh,</hi> with their days: and <foreign lang="ar">العَشْرُ</foreign>, alone, to <hi rend="ital">The</hi> first <hi rend="ital">ten</hi> nights of El-Moharram, with their days.] The Arabs also said, <foreign lang="ar">سِرْنَا عَشْرًا</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">We journeyed ten</hi> nights, with their days; making the fem. [<foreign lang="ar">لَيَالٍ</foreign>] to predominate over the masc. [<foreign lang="ar">أَيَّام</foreign>]; as is the case in the Kur ii. 234. (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">أَيَّامُ العَشْرِ</foreign> is used for <foreign lang="ar">أَيَّامُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">اللَّيَالِى العَشْرِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The days of the ten nights</hi>]. (Mgh.) [See some other observations applying to the syntax of <foreign lang="ar">عَشَرَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَشْرٌ</foreign>, voce <foreign lang="ar">خَمْسَةٌ</foreign>. And respecting a peculiar pronunciation of the people of El-Hijáz, and a case in which <foreign lang="ar">عَشَرَة</foreign> is imperfectly decl., see <foreign lang="ar">ثَلَاثَةٌ</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [<foreign lang="ar">عَشْرٌ</foreign> is also applied to <hi rend="ital">A portion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">paragraph, of the Kur-án properly consisting of ten verses;</hi> but it is often applied to <hi rend="ital">somewhat more,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">less, than what is considered by some,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by all, as ten verses,</hi> either because there is much disagreement as to the divisions of the verses or for the sake of beginning and ending with a break in the tenour of the text: (see <foreign lang="ar">عَاشِرَةٌ</foreign>:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">أَعْشَارٌ</foreign>. These divisions have no mark to distinguish them in some MSS.: in others, each is marked by a round ornament at the end; or by the word <foreign lang="ar">عشر</foreign>, or the letter <foreign lang="ar">ع</foreign>, over, or over against, the commencement.]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  When you have passed the number ten, you make the masc. fem., and the fem. masc. [to nineteen inclusively]: in the masc., you reject the <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign> in <foreign lang="ar">عَشَرَة</foreign>; and from thirteen to nineteen [inclusively], you add <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign> to the former of the two nouns; and [in every case] you pronounce the <foreign lang="ar">ش</foreign> with fet-h; and you make the two nouns one noun, [and, as such,] indecl., with fet-h for the termination: (TA:) you say, <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدَ عَشَرَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Eleven</hi>], (S, O, Msb,) [and <foreign lang="ar">اِثْنَا عَشَرَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Twelve,</hi>] and <foreign lang="ar">ثَلَاثَةَ عَشَرَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Thirteen</hi>], and so on; (Msb, TA;) with fet-h to the <foreign lang="ar">ش</foreign>; and in one dial. with sukoon [<foreign lang="ar">أَحَدَ عَشْرَ</foreign>, &amp;c.]; (Msb;) or the former only: (S, O:) and, as ISk says, some of the Arabs make the <foreign lang="ar">ع</foreign> quiescent, [as many do in the present day,] saying <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدَ عْشَرَ</foreign>, and so on to <foreign lang="ar">تِسْعَةَ عْشَرَ</foreign> [inclusively] except in the instance of <foreign lang="ar">اِثْنَا عَشَرَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">اِثْنَىْ عَشَرَ</foreign>, because of the quiescence of the <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>; and Akh says that they make the <foreign lang="ar">ع</foreign> quiescent because the noun is long and its vowels are many: (S, O) in the fem., you add <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign> to the latter of the two nouns, and reject the <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign> in the former of them, and make the <foreign lang="ar">ش</foreign> in <foreign lang="ar">عشرة</foreign> quiescent: you say <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى عَشْرَةَ</foreign> (TA,) [and <foreign lang="ar">اِثْنَتَا</foreign>

                  <hi rend="ital">A company,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">collective body,</hi> (Az, S, O, Msb, K,) <hi rend="ital">of people,</hi> (S,) <hi rend="ital">consisting of men, exclusive of women;</hi> like <foreign lang="ar">نَفَرٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">قَوْمٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">رَهْطٌ</foreign>; (Az, Msb;) having no proper sing.: (Az:) or <hi rend="ital">any company,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">collective body, whose state of circumstances is one; a community;</hi> as the <foreign lang="ar">معشر</foreign> of the Muslims and that of the Polytheists: (Lth:) or <hi rend="ital">a great company,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">collective body;</hi> so called [from <foreign lang="ar">عَشَرَةٌ</foreign>,] because they are many; for <foreign lang="ar">عشرة</foreign> is that large and perfect number after which there is no number but what is composed of the units comprised in it: (MF:) or the <hi rend="ital">family</hi> of a man: or <hi rend="ital">jinn</hi> (i. e. <hi rend="ital">genii</hi>) <hi rend="ital">and mankind:</hi> (K: [or the author of the K may mean, or <hi rend="ital">jinn:</hi> and also <hi rend="ital">mankind:</hi>]) in the Kur [vi. 130, and lv. 33], we find the expression <foreign lang="ar">يَا مَعْشَرَ ٱلْجِنِّ وَٱلْإِنْسِ</foreign>; but this means <hi rend="ital">O</hi>

                  <hi rend="ital">consisting of the jinn and of mankind:</hi> and [vi. 128], <foreign lang="ar">يَا مَعْشَرَ الجِنِّ</foreign>, without the mention of <foreign lang="ar">الانس</foreign>: (MF:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">مَعَاشِرُ</foreign>. (S, Msb.) [See also <foreign lang="ar">عَشِيرَةٌ</foreign>.]       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">مَعْشَرَ</foreign>: see <foreign lang="ar">عُشَارَ</foreign>, in four places.
